 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Advertising&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Stock-Based Compensation&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company accounts for stock-based&#13;compensation in accordance with ASC Topic 718, &amp;#147;Compensation &amp;#150; Stock Compensation&amp;#148; (&amp;#147;ASC 718&amp;#148;) which&#13;establishes financial accounting and reporting standards for stock-based employee compensation. It defines a fair value based method&#13;of accounting for an employee stock option or similar equity instrument. The Company accounts for compensation cost for stock option&#13;plans in accordance with ASC 718. The Company accounts for share-based payments to non-employees in accordance with ASC 505-50&#13;&amp;#147;Equity Based Payments to Non-Employees&amp;#148;.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company recognizes all forms of&#13;share-based payments, including stock option grants, warrants and restricted stock grants, at their fair value on the grant date,&#13;which are based on the estimated number of awards that are ultimately expected to vest.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Share-based payments, excluding restricted&#13;stock, are valued using a Black-Scholes option pricing model. Grants of share-based payment awards issued to non-employees for&#13;services rendered have been recorded at the fair value of the share-based payment, which is the more readily determinable value.&#13;The grants are amortized on a straight-line basis over the requisite service periods, which is generally the vesting period. If&#13;an award is granted, but vesting does not occur, any previously recognized compensation cost is reversed in the period related&#13;to the termination of service. Stock-based compensation expenses are included in cost of goods sold or selling, general and administrative&#13;expenses, depending on the nature of the services provided, in the consolidated statement of operations. Share-based payments issued&#13;to placement agents are classified as a direct cost of a stock offering and are recorded as a reduction in additional paid in capital.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For the year ended January 31, 2016&#13;and 2015, share-based compensation amounted to $487,316 and $438,343, respectively. Of the $487,316, and $438,343 recorded for&#13;the year ended January 31, 2016 and 2015, $241,769 and $171,981 were direct costs of a stock offering and have been recorded as&#13;a reduction in additional paid in capital.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Times

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The expected option term is computed&#13;using the &amp;#147;simplified&amp;#148; method as permitted under the provisions of ASC 718-10-599. The Company uses the simplified&#13;method to calculate expected term of share options and similar instruments as the Company does not have sufficient historical exercise&#13;data to provide a reasonable basis upon which to estimate expected term.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Earnings (Loss) Per Share&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Basic earnings (loss) per share is computed&#13;by dividing net income (loss) by the weighted average number of shares of common stock outstanding during each period. Diluted&#13;earnings (loss) per share is computed by dividing net income (loss), adjusted for changes in income or loss that resulted from&#13;the assumed conversion of convertible shares, by the weighted average number of shares of common stock, common stock equivalents&#13;and potentially dilutive securities outstanding during the period.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Income taxes are provided in accordance&#13;with ASC No. 740, &amp;#147;Accounting for Income Taxes&amp;#148;. A deferred tax asset or liability is recorded for all temporary differences&#13;between financial and tax reporting and net operating loss carryforwards. Deferred tax expense (benefit) results from the net change&#13;during the period of deferred tax assets and liabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Deferred tax assets are reduced by a&#13;valuation allowance when, in the opinion of management, it is more likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax&#13;assets will not be realized. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are adjusted for the effects of changes in tax laws and rates&#13;on the date of enactment.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Reclassification&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Recent Accounting Pronouncements&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2014, the Financial Accounting&#13;Standards Board (&amp;#147;FASB&amp;#148;) issued Accounting Standards Update (ASU) No. 2014-09, Revenue from Contracts with Customers.&#13;The revenue recognition standard affects all entities that have contracts with customers, except for certain items. The new revenue&#13;recognition standard eliminates the transaction and industry-specific revenue recognition guidance under current GAAP and replaces&#13;it with a principle-based approach for determining revenue recognition. In July 2015, the effective date was delayed one year by&#13;a vote by the FASB. Public business entities, certain not-for-profit entities, and certain employee benefit plans would apply the&#13;guidance in ASU 2014-09 to annual reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2017, including interim reporting periods within&#13;that reporting period. Earlier application would be permitted only as of annual reporting periods beginning after December 15,&#13;2016, including interim reporting periods within that reporting period. The Company has reviewed the applicable ASU and has not,&#13;at the current time, quantified the effects of this pronouncement.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2015, the Financial Accounting&#13;Standards Board issued Accounting Standards Update (ASU) No. 2015-03, Interest - Imputation of Interest (Subtopic 835-30): Simplifying&#13;the Presentation of Debt Issuance Costs. The amendments in this ASU require that debt issuance costs related to a recognized debt&#13;liability be presented in the balance sheet as a direct deduction from the carrying amount of that debt liability, consistent with&#13;debt discounts. The recognition and measurement guidance for debt issuance costs are not affected by the amendments in this ASU.&#13;The amendments are effective for financial statements issued for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2015, and interim periods&#13;within those fiscal years. Early adoption of the amendments is permitted for financial statements that have not been previously&#13;issued. The amendments should be applied on a retrospective basis, wherein the balance sheet of each individual period presented&#13;should be adjusted to reflect the period-specific effects of applying the new guidance. Upon transition, an entity is required&#13;to comply with the applicable disclosures for a change in an accounting principle. These disclosures include the nature of and&#13;reason for the change in accounting principle, the transition method, a description of the prior-period information that has been&#13;retrospectively adjusted, and the effect of the change on the financial statement line items (i.e., debt issuance cost asset and&#13;the debt liability). The Company is currently evaluating the effects of ASU 2015-03 on the consolidated financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In July 2015, the FASB issued the FASB&#13;Accounting Standards Update No. 2015-11 &amp;#147;&lt;i&gt;Inventory (Topic 330)&lt;/i&gt;: &lt;i&gt;Simplifying the Measurement of Inventory&amp;#148;&#13;(&amp;#147;ASU 2015-11&amp;#148;). &lt;/i&gt;The amendments in this Update do not apply to inventory that is measured using last-in, first-out&#13;(LIFO) or the retail inventory method. The amendments apply to all other inventory, which includes inventory that is measured using&#13;first-in, first-out (FIFO) or average cost. An entity should measure inventory within the scope of this Update at the lower of&#13;cost and net realizable value. Net realizable value is the estimated selling prices in the ordinary course of business, less reasonably&#13;predictable costs of completion, disposal, and transportation. Subsequent measurement is unchanged for inventory measured using&#13;LIFO or the retail inventory method.&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;For public business entities, the amendments in this Update are effective for fiscal&#13;years beginning after December 15, 2016, including interim periods within those fiscal years. The Company is currently evaluating&#13;the effects of ASU 2015-11 on the consolidated financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August 2015, the FASB issued the&#13;FASB Accounting Standards Update No. 2015-14 &amp;#147;&lt;i&gt;Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606)&lt;/i&gt;: &lt;i&gt;Deferral of the&#13;Effective Date&amp;#148; (&amp;#147;ASU 2015-14&amp;#148;). &lt;/i&gt;The amendments in this Update defer the effective date of Update 2014-09&#13;for all entities by one year. Public business entities, certain not-for-profit entities, and certain employee benefit plans should&#13;apply the guidance in Update 2014-09 to annual reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2017, including interim reporting&#13;periods within that reporting period. Earlier application is permitted only as of annual reporting periods beginning after December&#13;15, 2016, including interim reporting periods within that reporting period. The Company is currently evaluating the effects of&#13;ASU 2015-14 on the consolidated financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.8pt&gt;In April 2015, the&#13;Financial Accounting Standards Board issued Accounting Standards Update 2015-03,&lt;i&gt; Interest-Imputation of Interest. &lt;/i&gt;To simplify&#13;presentation of debt issuance costs, the amendments in this Update would require that debt issuance costs be presented in the balance&#13;sheet as a direct deduction from the carrying amount of debt liability, consistent with debt discounts or premiums. The recognition&#13;and measurement guidance for debt issuance costs would not be affected by the amendments in this update. This Accounting Standards&#13;Update is the final version of Proposed Accounting Standards Update 2014-250-Interest-Imputation of Interest (Subtopic 835-30),&#13;which has been deleted. The amendments in this update are effective for financial statements issued for fiscal years beginning&#13;after December 15, 2015, and interim periods within those fiscal years. The adoption of ASU 2015-03 is not expected to have a material&#13;impact on our financial position, results of operations or cash flows.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In February 2016, the Financial Accounting&#13;Standards Board (&amp;#147;FASB&amp;#148;) issued Accounting Standards Update (&amp;#147;ASU&amp;#148;) No. 2016-02, &amp;#147;Leases&amp;#148; (topic&#13;842). The FASB issued this update to increase transparency and comparability among organizations by recognizing lease assets and&#13;lease liabilities on the balance sheet and disclosing key information about leasing arrangements. The updated guidance is effective&#13;for annual periods beginning after December 15, 2018, including interim periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption of the&#13;update is permitted. The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2016, the Financial Accounting&#13;Standards Board (&amp;#147;FASB&amp;#148;) issued Accounting Standards Update (&amp;#147;ASU&amp;#148;) No. 2016-06, &amp;#147;Derivatives and&#13;Hedging&amp;#148; (topic 815). The FASB issued this update to clarify the requirements for assessing whether contingent call (put)&#13;options that can accelerate the payment of principal on debt instruments are clearly and closely related to their debt hosts. An&#13;entity performing the assessment under the amendments in this update is required to assess the embedded call (put) options solely&#13;in accordance with the four-step decision sequence. The updated guidance is effective for annual periods beginning after December&#13;15, 2016, including interim periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption of the update is permitted. The Company is currently&#13;evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In April 2016, the Financial Accounting&#13;Standards Board (&amp;#147;FASB&amp;#148;) issued Accounting Standards Update (&amp;#147;ASU&amp;#148;) No. 2016-09, &amp;#147;Compensation &amp;#150;&#13;Stock Compensation&amp;#148; (topic 718). The FASB issued this update to improve the accounting for employee share-based payments&#13;and affect all organizations that issue share-based payment awards to their employees. Several aspects of the accounting for share-based&#13;payment award transactions are simplified, including: (a) income tax consequences; (b) classification of awards as either equity&#13;or liabilities; and (c) classification on the statement of cash flows. The updated guidance is effective for annual periods beginning&#13;after December 15, 2016, including interim periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption of the update is permitted. The Company&#13;is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Inventories are stated at average cost&#13;using the first-in, first-out (FIFO) valuation method. Inventory was comprised of the following at January 31, 2016 and January&#13;31, 2015:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Property and equipment on January 31,&#13;2016 and 2015 are as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 4 - Investment in Meatball&#13;Obsession, LLC&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During 2011 the Company acquired a 34.62%&#13;interest in Meatball Obsession, LLC (&amp;#147;MO&amp;#148;) for a total investment of $27,032. This investment is accounted for using&#13;the equity method of accounting. Accordingly, investments are recorded at acquisition cost plus the Company&amp;#146;s equity in the&#13;undistributed earnings or losses of the entity.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;At December 31, 2011 the investment&#13;was written down to $0 due to losses incurred by MO.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 5 - Related Party Transactions&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Joseph Epstein Foods&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On March 1, 2010, the Company entered&#13;into a five year agreement with Joseph Epstein Foods (the &amp;#147;Manufacturer&amp;#148;) who is a related party. The Manufacturer&#13;is co-owned by the CEO and President of the Company. The Company analyzed the relationship with the Manufacturer to determine if&#13;the Manufacturer is a variable interest entity as defined by FASB ASC 810 &amp;#147;Consolidation&amp;#148;. Based on this analysis,&#13;the Company has determined that the Manufacturer is a variable interest entity but the Company is not the primary beneficiary of&#13;the variable interest entity and therefore consolidation is not required. In addition, based on the analysis the Company determined&#13;that the CEO and President of the Company is the primary beneficiary of the variable interest entity and bears the risk of loss.&#13;Under the terms of the agreement, the Company grants to the Manufacturer a revocable license to use the Company&amp;#146;s recipes,&#13;formulas, methods and ingredients for the preparation and production of Company&amp;#146;s products, for manufacturing the Company&amp;#146;s&#13;product and all future improvements, modifications, substitutions and replacements developed by the Company. The Manufacturer in&#13;turn grants the Company the exclusive right to purchase the product. Under the terms of the agreement the Manufacturer agrees to&#13;manufacture, package, and store the Company&amp;#146;s products and the Company has the right to purchase products from one or more&#13;other manufacturers, distributors or suppliers. The agreement contains a perpetual automatic renewal clause for a period of one&#13;year after the expiration of the initial term. During the renewal period either party may cancel the contract with written notice&#13;nine months prior to the termination date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Under the terms of the agreement if&#13;the Company specifies any change in packaging or shipping materials which results in the manufacturer incurring increased expense&#13;for packaging and shipping materials or in the Manufacturer being unable to utilize obsolete packaging or shipping materials in&#13;ordinary packaging or shipping, the Company agrees to pay as additional product cost the additional cost for packaging and shipping&#13;materials and to purchase at cost such obsolete packaging and shipping materials. If the Company requests any repackaging of the&#13;product, other than due to defects in the original packaging, the Company will reimburse the Manufacturer for any labor costs incurred&#13;in repackaging. Per the agreement, all product delivery shipping costs are the expense of the Company. The Company agreed with&#13;the Manufacturer at the end of the last fiscal year that Company would purchase a minimum of $933,000 of product each month and&#13;that any amount below that sum would be a charge of 12% of that shortfall each month. In return, the Manufacturer obligated itself&#13;to offer the Company competitive prices and would not co-pack for other suppliers and would either maintain or lower its payable&#13;to the Company each quarter. In addition, the Manufacturer agreed to rebate the Company any overage of gross margin above 12% each&#13;month.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;From time to time the Company will make&#13;improvements to the Manufacturer&amp;#146;s facility. The improvements are capitalized and depreciated over the estimated useful life.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the year ended January 31, 2016&#13;and 2015, the Company purchased inventory of $8,381,441 and $8,907,380, respectively, from the Manufacturer.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the year ended January 31, 2016&#13;and 2015, the Manufacturer incurred expenses of $24,000 and $48,000, respectively, on behalf of the Company for shared administrative&#13;expenses and salary expenses.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;At January 31, 2016 and January 31,&#13;2015, the amount due from the Manufacturer is $2,248,781 and $2,213,037, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Meatball Obsession, LLC&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;A current director of the Company is&#13;the chairman of the board and shareholder of Meatball Obsession LLC (&amp;#147;MO&amp;#148;).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For the year ended January 31, 2016&#13;and 2015, the Company generated approximately $67,120 and $113,600 in revenues from MO, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;As of January 31, 2016 and 2015, the&#13;Company had a receivable of $6,512 and $6,768 due from MO, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;WWS, Inc.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;A current director of the Company is&#13;the president of WWS, Inc.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For the year ended January 31, 2016&#13;and 2015, the Company recorded $48,000 and $48,000 in commission expense from WWS, Inc. generated sales, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Notes Payable&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 7 - Line of Credit&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Effective January 3, 2014, the Company&#13;entered into a Sale and Security Agreement (the &amp;#147;Sale and Security Agreement&amp;#148;) with Faunus Group International, Inc.&#13;(&amp;#147;FGI&amp;#148;) to provide for a $1.5 million secured demand credit facility backed by its receivables and inventory (the &amp;#147;FGI&#13;Facility&amp;#148;). The Sale and Security Agreement has an initial three year term (the &amp;#147;Original Term&amp;#148;) and shall be&#13;extended automatically for an additional one year for each succeeding term unless written notice of termination is given by either&#13;party at least sixty days prior to the end of the Original Term or any extension thereof. The Company and certain of its affiliates&#13;also entered into guarantees to guarantee the performance of the obligations under the Sale and Security Agreement (the &amp;#147;Guaranty&#13;Agreements&amp;#148;). The Company also granted FGI a security interest in and lien upon all of the Company&amp;#146;s right, title and&#13;interest in and to all of its assets (as defined in the Sale and Security Agreement).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Pursuant to the FGI Facility, FGI can&#13;elect to purchase eligible accounts receivables (&amp;#147;Purchased Accounts&amp;#148;) up to 70% of the value of such receivables (retaining&#13;a 30% reserve). At FGI&amp;#146;s election, FGI may advance the Company up to 70% of the value of any Purchased Accounts, subject&#13;to the FGI Facility. Reserves retained by FGI on any Purchased Accounts are expected to be refunded to the Company net of interest&#13;and fees on advances once the receivables are collected from customers. The interest rate on advances or borrowings under the FGI&#13;Facility will be the greater of (i) 6.75% per annum and (ii) 2.50% above the prime rate. Any advances or borrowings under the FGI&#13;Facility are due on demand.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company also agreed to pay to FGI&#13;monthly collateral management fees of 0.42% of the average monthly balance of Purchased Accounts. The minimum monthly net funds&#13;employed during each contract year hereof shall be $500,000. Additionally, the Company paid FGI a one-time facility fee equal to&#13;1% of the FGI Facility upon entry into the Sale and Security Agreement.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the year ended January 31, 2015,&#13;the Company terminated its agreement with FGI and paid off all obligations due at the payoff date. Upon termination, additional&#13;fees and accrued interest of approximately $48,600 were paid and included in the interest expense.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 8 - Loan and Security Agreement&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On September 3, 2014, the Company entered&#13;into a Loan and Security Agreement (&amp;#147;Loan and Security Agreement&amp;#148;) with Entrepreneur Growth Capital, LLC (&amp;#147;EGC&amp;#148;).&#13;The total facility is for an aggregate principal amount of up to $3,100,000. The facility consists of the following:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom; background-color: #CCEEFF&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 2%; text-align: justify; line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#9679;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 1%; line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 81%; line-height: 115%&gt;Accounts Revolving Line of Credit:&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 1%; line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 1%; line-height: 115%&gt;$&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 13%; text-align: right; line-height: 115%&gt;2,150,000&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 1%; line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom; background-color: white&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify; line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#9679;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;Inventory Revolving Line of Credit:&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;$&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right; line-height: 115%&gt;350,000&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom; background-color: #CCEEFF&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify; line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#9679;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;Term Loan:&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;$&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right; line-height: 115%&gt;600,000&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;EGC may from time to time make loans&#13;in an aggregate amount not to exceed the Accounts Revolving Line of Credit up to 85% of the net amount of Eligible Accounts (as&#13;defined in the Loan and Security Agreement). EGC may from time to time make loans in an aggregate amount not to exceed the Inventory&#13;Revolving Line of Credit against Eligible Inventory (as defined in the Loan and Security Agreement) in an amount up to 50% of finished&#13;goods and in an amount up to 20% of raw material.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The revolving interest rates is equal&#13;to the highest prime rate in effect during each month as generally reported by Citibank, N.A. plus (a) 2.5% on loans and advances&#13;made against eligible accounts and (b) 4.0% on loans made against eligible inventory. The term loan bears interest at a rate of&#13;the highest prime rate in effect during each month as generally reported by Citibank, N.A. plus 4.0%. The initial term of the facility&#13;is for a period of two years and will automatically renew for an additional one year period. The Company is required to pay a one-time&#13;facility fee equal to 2.25% of the total $3,100,000 facility. In the event of default, the Company shall pay 10% above the stated&#13;rates of interest per the Agreement. The drawdowns are secured by all of the assets of the Company.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;As of January 31, 2016 and 2015, the&#13;outstanding balance on the line of credit was $959,621 and $1,409,098, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On September 3, 2014, the Company also&#13;entered into a 5 year $600,000 Secured Promissory Note (&amp;#147;EGC Note&amp;#148;) with EGC. The EGC Note is payable in 60 monthly&#13;installments of $10,000. The EGC Note bears interest at the prime rate plus 4.0% and is payable monthly, in arrears. In the event&#13;of default, the Company shall pay 10% above the stated rates of interest per the Loan and Security Agreement. The EGC Note is secured&#13;by all of the assets of the Company. The outstanding balance on the term loan was $440,000 and $560,000 as of January 31, 2016&#13;and 2015, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in; background-color: white&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 6 - Promissory Notes&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On October 31, 2015, the Company entered&#13;into a promissory note agreement with a third party to settle outstanding payables. The note is for a total principal balance of&#13;$358,832, bearing interest at a rate of 10% and maturing in October 2017. The Company is required to prepay the note 10% of the&#13;net proceeds received upon the closing of a capital raise, except for, those transactions conducted with the Company&amp;#146;s Chief&#13;Executive Officer. The Company paid $119,373 toward the outstanding balance, a portion of which is 10% of the net proceeds from&#13;the final closing of the private placement in November 2015.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In January 2016, the Company entered&#13;into a promissory note agreement with a third party to settle outstanding payables. The note is for a total principal balance of&#13;$116,003, bearing interest at a rate of 6% and maturing in October 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 10 - Concentrations&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Revenues&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the year ended January 31, 2016,&#13;the Company earned revenues from four customers representing approximately 16%, 14%, 13% and 10% of gross sales. As of January&#13;31, 2016, these customers represented approximately 18%, 7%, 9% and 30% of total gross outstanding receivables, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the year ended January 31, 2015,&#13;the Company earned revenues from three customers representing approximately 18%, 13% and 11% of gross sales. As of January 31,&#13;2015, these customers represented approximately 23%, 12% and 15% of total gross outstanding receivables, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Risks and Uncertainties&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company operates in an industry&#13;that is subject to intense competition and change in consumer demand. The Company&amp;#146;s operations are subject to significant&#13;risk and uncertainties including financial and operational risks including the potential risk of business failure.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 9 - Convertible Note&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On December 19, 2014, the Company entered&#13;into a securities purchase agreement (the &amp;#147;Manatuck Purchase Agreement&amp;#148;) with Manatuck Hill Partners, LLC (&amp;#147;Manatuck&amp;#148;)&#13;whereby the Company issued a convertible redeemable debenture (the &amp;#147;Manatuck Debenture&amp;#148;) in favor of Manatuck. The&#13;Manatuck Debenture is for $2,000,000 bearing interest at a rate of 14% and matures in February 2016. Upon issuance of the Manatuck&#13;Debenture, the Company granted Manatuck 200,000 shares of the Company&amp;#146;s restricted common stock. In April 2015, the maturity&#13;date was extended to May 2016 and 30,000 shares of restricted common stock were issued to Manatuck. Based on management&amp;#146;s&#13;review, the accounting for debt modification applied. The Company valued the 30,000 shares at the grant date share price of $1.32&#13;and recorded $39,600 to debt discount on the consolidated balance sheet.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Upon issuance of the debenture and subsequent&#13;extension, a debt discount of $498,350 was recorded for the fees incurred by the buyer as well as the value of the common shares&#13;granted to Manatuck. The debt discount will be amortized over the earlier of (i) the term of the debt or (ii) conversion of the&#13;debt, using the straight-line method which approximates the effective interest method. The amortization of debt discount is included&#13;as a component of interest expense in the consolidated statements of operations. There was unamortized debt discount of $0 and&#13;$412,553 as of January 31, 2016 and 2015, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On October 29, 2015, the note was further&#13;amended to extend the maturity date to December 19, 2016. Per the terms of the execution of the extension, the Company was required&#13;to purchase the above 230,000 shares issued to Manatuck for a share price of $0.65, a value of $149,500 and incurred an amendment&#13;fee of $170,500, both of which were added to the outstanding principal of the debt. In addition, the extension reduced accrued&#13;interest by $220,000 and increased the outstanding principal of the debt by $220,000. The outstanding principal at January 31,&#13;2016 was $2,540,000. Based on management&amp;#146;s review, the accounting for debt extinguishment applied. In accordance with the&#13;accounting for debt extinguishment, the Company wrote-off the existing debt of $2,000,000, wrote-off the unamortized debt discount&#13;of $190,483 and wrote-off the remaining debt issuance costs relating to this note of $19,106. The loss on debt extinguishment of&#13;$380,089 on the statement of operations is comprised of the write-off of the remaining debt discount of $190,483, the write-off&#13;of the debt issuance costs of $19,106, and the amendment fee of $170,500.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Optional conversion to convertible preferred&#13;stock is available upon completion of a qualified offering (as defined in the Manatuck Purchase Agreement) while the Manatuck Debenture&#13;is outstanding. Upon conversion of the Manatuck Debenture, the Company shall issue Manatuck shares of common stock as defined in&#13;the Manatuck Purchase Agreement.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has U.S. federal net operating&#13;loss carryovers (NOLs) of approximately $12.9M and $8.8M at January 31, 2016 and 2015, respectively, available to offset taxable&#13;income through 2034. If not used, these NOLs may be subject to limitation under Internal Revenue Code Section 382 should there&#13;be a greater than 50% ownership change as determined under the regulations. The Company plans on undertaking a detailed analysis&#13;of any historical and/or current Section 382 ownership changes that may limit the utilization of the net operating loss carryovers.&#13;The Company also has New Jersey State Net Operating Loss carry overs of $12.9M and $8.8M at January 31, 2016 and 2015, respectively,&#13;available to offset future taxable income through 2034.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In assessing the realization of deferred&#13;tax assets, management considers whether it is more likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax assets will not&#13;be realized. The ultimate realization of deferred tax assets is dependent upon future generation for taxable income during the&#13;periods in which temporary differences representing net future deductible amounts become deductible. Management considers the scheduled&#13;reversal of deferred tax liabilities, projected future taxable income and tax planning strategies in making this assessment. After&#13;consideration of all the information available, Management believes that significant uncertainty exists with respect to future&#13;realization of the deferred tax assets and has therefore established a full valuation allowance. For the year ended January 31,&#13;2016 and 2015, the change in the valuation allowance was $1,405,640and $1,745,469.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company evaluated the provisions&#13;of ASC 740 related to the accounting for uncertainty in income taxes recognized in an enterprise&amp;#146;s financial statements.&#13;ASC 740 prescribes a comprehensive model for how a company should recognize, present, and disclose uncertain positions that the&#13;Company has taken or expects to take in its tax return. For those benefits to be recognized, a tax position must be more-likely-than-not&#13;to be sustained upon examination by taxing authorities. Differences between tax positions taken or expected to be taken in a tax&#13;return and the net benefit recognized and measured pursuant to the interpretation are referred to as &amp;#147;unrecognized benefits.&amp;#148;&#13;A liability is recognized (or amount of net operating loss carry forward or amount of tax refundable is reduced) for unrecognized&#13;tax benefit because it represents an enterprise&amp;#146;s potential future obligation to the taxing authority for a tax position&#13;that was not recognized as a result of applying the provisions of ASC 740.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;If applicable, interest costs related&#13;to the unrecognized tax benefits are required to be calculated and would be classified as &amp;#147;Other expenses &amp;#150; Interest&amp;#148;&#13;in the statement of operations. Penalties would be recognized as a component of &amp;#147;General and administrative.&amp;#148;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;No interest or penalties on unpaid tax&#13;were recorded during the year ended January 31, 2016 and 2015, respectively. As of January 31, 2016 and 2015, no liability for&#13;unrecognized tax benefits was required to be reported. The Company does not expect any significant changes in its unrecognized&#13;tax benefits in the next year.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The income tax provision (benefit) consists&#13;of the following:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company&amp;#146;s deferred tax assets&#13;(liabilities) consisted of the effects of temporary differences attributable to the following:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The expected tax expense (benefit) based&#13;on the statutory rate is reconciled with actual tax expense benefit as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 1 - Nature of Operations and Basis&#13;of Presentation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Nature of Operations&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;MamaMancini&amp;#146;s Holdings, Inc. (the &amp;#147;Company&amp;#148;),&#13;(formerly known as Mascot Properties, Inc.) was organized on July 22, 2009 as a Nevada corporation. The Company has a year end&#13;of January 31.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company is a manufacturer and distributor&#13;of beef meatballs with sauce, turkey meatballs with sauce, and other similar meats and sauces. The Company&amp;#146;s customers are&#13;located throughout the United States, with a large concentration in the Northeast and Southeast.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Basis of Presentation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The consolidated financial statements and related&#13;notes have been prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America (&amp;#147;US&#13;GAAP&amp;#148;) and include the accounts of the Company and its wholly-owned subsidiaries. All material intercompany balances and&#13;transactions have been eliminated in consolidation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Going Concern&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #252525; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #252525&gt;The accompanying financial&#13;statements have been prepared assuming that the Company will continue as a going concern. The Company incurred a loss of $3,511,618&#13;and $4,060,476 during the years ended January 31, 2016 and 2015, respectively. Also, as of January 31, 2016, the Company had $587,422&#13;in cash, and current liabilities exceeded current assets by $60,985. These factors all raise substantial doubt about the ability&#13;of the Company to continue as a going concern. In their report for the fiscal year ended January 31, 2016, the Company&amp;#146;s&#13;auditors have expressed an opinion that, as a result of the conditions noted, there is substantial doubt regarding the ability&#13;to continue as a going concern.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #252525; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
